    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f9f37023-0322-4c85-ac2d-9596115d41ff'

<div id="review_1952889076" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1952889076" />
    <a title="Lois Bujold" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7672661-lois-bujold"><img alt="Lois Bujold" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442449462p2/7672661.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1952889076?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lois Bujold" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lois Bujold" href="/user/show/7672661-lois-bujold">Lois Bujold</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316076074" href="/book/show/6405972-pandora-hearts-volume-1">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">manga readers and those interested in strange Japanese takes on Alice in Wonderland</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Lois by: </span>
      random internet review mentioned the smart character
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1952889076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5365917717084737476">OK, the week I was recovering from surgery on a really <i>generous</i> prescription for narcotic pain relievers was possibly not the optimum one for tacking this series. But I did.<br/><br/>Excellent artwork. Shall leave descriptions of set-up and plot to other reviewers. Pretty much all of the characters, protag and antag, were idiots, doing idiot things (granted usually with inadequate information) to advance the plot at a suitable clip. The one character who very much wasn't an idiot spent half his time prete</span>
  <span id="freeText5365917717084737476" style="display:none">OK, the week I was recovering from surgery on a really <i>generous</i> prescription for narcotic pain relievers was possibly not the optimum one for tacking this series. But I did.<br /><br />Excellent artwork. Shall leave descriptions of set-up and plot to other reviewers. Pretty much all of the characters, protag and antag, were idiots, doing idiot things (granted usually with inadequate information) to advance the plot at a suitable clip. The one character who very much wasn't an idiot spent half his time pretending to be, but I nonetheless plowed through all 24 volumes (22, as it turned out) in pursuit of his story. I was toward the middle tempted to start treating it all as I had <i>War and Peace</i> as a young reader, paging through to pick up Pierre's scenes and just reading them, which turned that tome into something much more manageable. But I figured I'd miss too much set-up.<br /><br />Also, the narrative rewards at the end were not well-distributed. Vincent Nightray should have died in a fire, frankly. And Xerxes Break should have won his princess (and she him.) They'd certainly earned each other. Presumably some fanficcer somewhere has corrected this.<br /><br />Oh, a note on the anime. For most of the two seasons it follows the manga closely enough to be near-interchangeable, but only gets about halfway through the story. The last three episodes of season 2 are utter gibberish slapped in by the anime people when, I posit, they were told it wasn't to be renewed, so they tried (and failed) to fake up some closure. Skip those last episodes. The rest is OK.<br /><br />Ta, L.<br /><br />Addendum: Having been drawn into revisiting this work, I should add that while the work-as-a-whole merely whelmed me, the character of Xerxes "Learn From My Fail" Break gets five stars.<br /><br />Later still: raising this to <s>4</s> 5 stars because it got me to read it through <s>twice</s> *coughmany* times, if one counts the re-skimming. Partly to try out my new tablet for manga (brilliant), partly to see if it would make more sense if I gave it a fairer reading not treating most of the rest of the cast and their problems as speed bumps between me and my character of interest. Also with fewer drugs. Well, hm. I'd say it pretty much requires two readings just to sort out the event salad, multi-layered flashbacks and cutting for suspense and so on, only partly due to how the Abyss screws with time.<br /><br />For all the furniture from <i>Alice in Wonderland</i>, the core story here turns out to be <i>Pinocchio</i>, curiously enough.<br /><br />Xerxes remains the smartest man in the room, or even more so, Reim's diligence and Barma's slyness notwithstanding -- or perhaps the wisest, all hard-won. But I have to take back my earlier remarks about narrative rewards. He entirely earned his character arc, every heartbreaking bit of it, and he would be diminished if it were to be taken from him. Dammit. Which was part of the thematic point of the whole structure. Also, I don't see how this is a work for children. (Possibly for grownups emotionally scarred as children by that Disney movie.) At the very least, I suspect younger readers would process events and character remarks very differently from their seniors. Which is kind of a given for any work of fiction, but might be more visible here.<br /><br />Interesting, reading the end-matter, I discovered its creation took, and took place over, nine years. Speaking as a creator myself, yeepers.<br /><br />Also, speaking of gendered fiction, it made an interesting compare-and-contrast with <i>Bleach</i>, also recently revisited. The two 15-year-old male protagonists could scarcely be less alike. Much to consider on that one.<br /><br />Ta, L.<br /><br />... Also, does anyone else suspect the Rainsworth women reproduce by parthenogenesis...?</span>
  <a data-text-id="5365917717084737476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_380581163" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/380581163" />
    <a title="Amy Keeley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7249971-amy-keeley"><img alt="Amy Keeley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442625121p2/7249971.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/380581163?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy Keeley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy Keeley" href="/user/show/7249971-amy-keeley">Amy Keeley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of complex plot, complex characters, surreal worlds</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7249971-amy-keeley?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer380581163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9116914286912437532">I cannot begin to describe how amazing this series is. But because you probably want to know why I gave this series five stars, I'll try.<br/><br/>First, the artwork is gorgeous. Whether it's an action scene, an emotional moment, or horror and madness, the artwork always delivers. Though the comic relief isn't as frequent as some other series, it's well done. What could have easily been jarring flows just as well as the rest of the plot.<br/><br/>As for the story, I have never seen a more twisted take on Alice in W</span>
  <span id="freeText9116914286912437532" style="display:none">I cannot begin to describe how amazing this series is. But because you probably want to know why I gave this series five stars, I'll try.<br /><br />First, the artwork is gorgeous. Whether it's an action scene, an emotional moment, or horror and madness, the artwork always delivers. Though the comic relief isn't as frequent as some other series, it's well done. What could have easily been jarring flows just as well as the rest of the plot.<br /><br />As for the story, I have never seen a more twisted take on Alice in Wonderland. Ever. And the beauty of it is that Jun Mochizuki does this without taking away the sense of wonder and innocence involved in discovering a world that isn't what you thought it was. The Abyss is terrifying, but it's also, in a way, beautiful.<br /><br />(I want to clarify something though. This is not a re-telling of Alice in Wonderland or a variation on it. The plot uses elements from AiW to tell a completely original story.)<br /><br />Oz is a wonderfully engaging character. On the one hand, he accepts everything, including the craziness of the Abyss, very easily. He seems happy-go-lucky and careless, but it doesn't take long to realize he's hiding emotional scars. Between that and his surprising intelligence, he's a joy to watch in action.<br /><br />Alice, a Chain from the Abyss also known as B-Rabbit, and Oz's contractee, is, at various times, crazy, heartless, amazing, cunning, and surprisingly vulnerable. Even though she can kill without remorse, her time with Oz hints at a future humanity for the crazed rabbit.<br /><br />The first volume, for all its greatness, is still mostly set-up. Fantastic set-up (even now I'm pretty much speechless), but still only a beginning. And with a beginning like this, reading the next volume is almost inevitable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9116914286912437532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15220977991818714624">When I first started reading this book, my friend Chloe (who reccommended it to me) told me that "Everything I believed was true was in fact <i>wrong</i>."<br/>I'm sure there was more capslock in there. Regardless, back when I started this specific volume I had no idea of how much that would prove to be <i>absolutely correct</i>.<br/>I knew nothing.<br/>Because of this, I spent half of my time reading this manga going "What the fuck is going on?"<br/>And yet, even though everything was completely confusing for 60+ chapters (sorr</span>
  <span id="freeText15220977991818714624" style="display:none">When I first started reading this book, my friend Chloe (who reccommended it to me) told me that "Everything I believed was true was in fact <i>wrong</i>."<br />I'm sure there was more capslock in there. Regardless, back when I started this specific volume I had no idea of how much that would prove to be <i>absolutely correct</i>.<br />I knew nothing.<br />Because of this, I spent half of my time reading this manga going "What the fuck is going on?"<br />And yet, even though everything was completely confusing for 60+ chapters (sorry, Retraces), I couldn't stop reading.<br />It might have been the superbe characters. It might have been that Raven is the perfect bishonen and yet is also a beautiful subversion. It might have been that I have elected Oz "My Baby" and that Break is lovely and outrageous, that Sharon is the best, that Alice and I have very similar priorities.<br />It might have been that the art develops to become absolutely gorgeous.<br />Regardless, I'm happy that I kept reading.<br />I'm happy because this is an absolutely wonderful piece of writing. The plot is so complex and well paced that I am left stunned.<br />Who in the world can weave a story, make you believe certain things so firmly and then <i>completely turn all your certainties on their heads?</i> (And not as a cheap trick: as a studied, prepared, accounted for move, with its own foreshadowing that we were just too blind to see) Who can make me feel <i>physical pain</i> for a character? All the while drawing the most beautiful illustrations?<br />A damn fine writer and artist, that's who.<br />So much so that I just gave five stars to all volumes, and I ain't even mad.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1706207770" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1706207770" />
    <a title="ManiacalBookUnicorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30770336-maniacalbookunicorn"><img alt="ManiacalBookUnicorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468119940p2/30770336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1706207770?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ManiacalBookUnicorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ManiacalBookUnicorn" href="/user/show/30770336-maniacalbookunicorn">ManiacalBookUnicorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316076074" href="/book/show/6405972-pandora-hearts-volume-1">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30770336-maniacalbookunicorn?shelf=manga">manga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30770336-maniacalbookunicorn?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1706207770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8733762262932386881"><b>"Those who come to the Abyss are all the same. They're all desperate to get something back. But everyone goes mad partway..."</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469410979ra/19814547.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>See, I really, really don’t understand how an author, mangaka, f-ing story writing genius, can immerse readers in something so gloriously messed up, beautiful, emo, crazy, funny, deep, and downright strange like it's nothing. More than just a few times I laughed out loud and shook my head thinking: psshh, that’s absolutely ridiculous and stupid, then turned the page only t</span>
  <span id="freeText8733762262932386881" style="display:none"><b>"Those who come to the Abyss are all the same. They're all desperate to get something back. But everyone goes mad partway..."</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469410979ra/19814547.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>See, I really, really don’t understand how an author, mangaka, f-ing story writing genius, can immerse readers in something so gloriously messed up, beautiful, emo, crazy, funny, deep, and downright strange like it's nothing. More than just a few times I laughed out loud and shook my head thinking: psshh, that’s absolutely ridiculous and stupid, then turned the page only to stop just short of curling up into a ball in a dark corner, gently caressing the book and whispering softly to it, while crying myself to sleep. How the heck can a person accomplish not looking like a mad person while reading this series (it’s not that I’m actually just crazy…honest)? This is just one of those books where you WILL get people whispering about you and strange, slightly fearful, glances if you read it in public, cause incomprehensible outbursts of emotion are a thing throughout this series.<br><br>Okay, now that I’m done with my rant, on with the review:<br><br>I honestly never expected to really like this series and wasn’t expecting much from it. I tried to watch the anime a couple years ago, but couldn’t really get into it (never made it past the first part of the 1st episode). After the first volume I figured I’d enjoy it, but it probably wouldn’t be a favorite. Once I got to the 4th volume I figured I’d really like it, but might not buy it (in my poor defense I’ve got a pretty extensive list of manga to buy so I’m really reluctant to add to it). But past that…I stopped caring about the total price of the series, food, and sleep. The last couple arcs almost killed me with all the FEELS.<br><br><b>"Finally I saw... A world so bright I almost wanted to cry... It was then, that my consciousness was engulfed in darkness."</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469410979ra/19814548.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I actually had to put the book down a few times and walk away in an attempt to take it all in, especially since I was usually still trying to deal with the aftermath of a few events/feels in previous arcs. Wait, my bad, I’m ranting again lol. Okay…<br><br>The Story: So if you don’t already know (it’s a pretty popular series for good reason), it's got an Alice in Wonderland type thing going on and explores pretty complex themes, primarily identity and existence and how things like the presence/absence of memory, human (or otherwise) bonds/connections, and the past can shape one's identity and sense of self.<br><br>And for the full review please visit my blog <a href="https://maniacalbookunicorn.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16883366075195357958"><b> "Your sin...is your very being.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418609091i/12845582._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>After seeing this series constantly mentioned on Youtube, Goodreads and by friends, I decided why the heck not? Then I saw the price. $13!? For each volume? And guess how many there are? (Japanese set was all I could find to show you.)<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418608669i/12845448.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>And that's not even all of them! It's ongoing so, naturally, one would run to the plentiful garden of scanlations!!!! Except, I don't read scanlations anymore. After reading about how little these mangaka's make, especially if they a</span>
  <span id="freeText16883366075195357958" style="display:none"><b> "Your sin...is your very being.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418609091i/12845582._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>After seeing this series constantly mentioned on Youtube, Goodreads and by friends, I decided why the heck not? Then I saw the price. $13!? For each volume? And guess how many there are? (Japanese set was all I could find to show you.)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418608669i/12845448.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And that's not even all of them! It's ongoing so, naturally, one would run to the plentiful garden of scanlations!!!! Except, I don't read scanlations anymore. After reading about how little these mangaka's make, especially if they are not one of the "Big 3", I decided that should I be serious about reading a series, I would purchase it. New. While it's nice to imagine a library...my wallet hates me.<br><br>Finally, I discovered Rightstuf. (I am not being paid to advertise them, I seriously do recommend them with all of my heart because I LOVE anime/manga and those who do as well know just how expensive that shit is!) I paid around $8-9 or so for each, and now have 6 volumes on my self. It's not much, but it did save me money and so far the series is intriguing.<br><br>Oz Vessalius is turning 15, and being the son of a rich duke, he has to attend a coming of age ceremony. Of course, everything goes wrong!:D<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418608669i/12845449._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Oz is pulled into the "Abyss" where criminals who commit terrible crimes are sent to rot. Oz's sin? His very existence. Soon after, he runs into Alice, who intervened in his ceremony as a black rabbit, and who also came into contact with him after he touched a locket he found on a mysterious grave. <br><br>Alice proceeds to issue a contract with Oz, which will get both of them out of the Abyss. After some trouble, they finally seal the contract-Kamisama Kiss style;)-and shit gets even more weird and confusing. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418608669i/12845450._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>There is definitely a bigger plot going on than what we have. Alice's whole reason to get out of the Abyss is to recover her scattered memories. Is she human? Is she a Chain? Is she a black rabbit? Or maybe she is even dead? (Just some assumptions) She is a badass, so us girls will be pleased with her character. She takes nothing from anyone, and will do what she has to. And Oz is very likable as well...yeah, I sort of have a thing for blonde guys :D <br><br>One question I have right now though: Who and where is Oz's dad? I have a feeling he was in the Ceremony, but can't be certain. <br><br>Allusions to Alice in Wonderland are very prominent in Pandora Hearts. We have The Mad Hatter ( pretty sure he is) Tweedle Dee and Dum, Alice and the rabbit. The art is absolutely GORGEOUS and I am looking forward to the Art Book that is coming out December 26.<br><br>The anime is not the manga, from what I know. The story suddenly changes and angered many fans.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418608669i/12845451._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Highly recommended but be aware that most things won't make a lot of sense right away.<br><br>You can purchase Pandora Hearts here from Rightstuf for $9.74 instead of $13:<br><a href="http://www.rightstuf.com/cgi-bin/catalogmgr/uo5YE5Xj0C7YvRPUqI/browse/item/84042/4/0/0" rel="nofollow noopener">my link</a></span>

<div id="review_240409292" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/240409292" />
    <a title="Kate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/757092-kate"><img alt="Kate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370216233p2/757092.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/240409292?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate" href="/user/show/757092-kate">Kate</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/757092-kate?shelf=8-pandora-hearts">8-pandora-hearts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/757092-kate?shelf=manga-total-volumes">manga-total-volumes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer240409292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1848848880102606884">I've been having neck pain lately, which keeps me up at night. So, I decided what better way to divert myself than by rereading a most excellent manga series?<br/><br/>Pandora Hearts is one of those series that I knew I would love once I gave it the time it was due. It's complex, both in plot and the way the story unfolds. It's easy to get lost between volumes (when you're waiting months in between releases). What makes it great, though, is that it's a really wonderful series for rereading. You simply can</span>
  <span id="freeText1848848880102606884" style="display:none">I've been having neck pain lately, which keeps me up at night. So, I decided what better way to divert myself than by rereading a most excellent manga series?<br /><br />Pandora Hearts is one of those series that I knew I would love once I gave it the time it was due. It's complex, both in plot and the way the story unfolds. It's easy to get lost between volumes (when you're waiting months in between releases). What makes it great, though, is that it's a really wonderful series for rereading. You simply cannot get bored. Since I had the basic plot and characters down on this reread, I was able to notice so many other details and nuances to the story. I love finding a series that does this to this level. I love studying the art, figuring out what the characters are thinking that words don't share with the reader. With so many vivid characters, this series is just a lot of fun (Xerxes Break's my favorite! But, I love Oz, too!)<br /><br />While rather dark (to the macabre at time), the art is striking and even beautiful. I have a thing for this Victorian-era-goth-esque design, so it may be personal preference, but I love the designs used for characters and setting. <br /><br />Highly recommended. Upgraded to 5 stars because it's really won me over at last.<br /><br /><br />*First read and reviewed on November 26, 2011 with 4 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1848848880102606884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3411163760" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3411163760" />
    <a title="Ren (A Bookish Balance)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15269781-ren-a-bookish-balance"><img alt="Ren (A Bookish Balance)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581906029p2/15269781.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3411163760?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ren (A Bookish Balance)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ren (A Bookish Balance)" href="/user/show/15269781-ren-a-bookish-balance">Ren (A Bookish Balance)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316076074" href="/book/show/6405972-pandora-hearts-volume-1">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15269781-ren-a-bookish-balance?shelf=series-unfinished">series-unfinished</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3411163760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9916289920967358537"><b>This review contains spoilers</b>.<br/><br/>4/5 stars<br/><br/><i>Pandora Hearts</i> is a Victorian inspired, steampunk fantasy story revolving around a mysterious prison called the Abyss. During Oz Vessalius's 15th birthday and coming-of-age ceremony he is condemned to the Abyss, his crime being his very existence. There he meets a mysterious young woman named Alice, and the two form a contract. In exchange for helping him out of the Abyss, Oz will help Alice regain her memories.<br/><br/>My initial impression after reading this first</span>
  <span id="freeText9916289920967358537" style="display:none"><b>This review contains spoilers</b>.<br /><br />4/5 stars<br /><br /><i>Pandora Hearts</i> is a Victorian inspired, steampunk fantasy story revolving around a mysterious prison called the Abyss. During Oz Vessalius's 15th birthday and coming-of-age ceremony he is condemned to the Abyss, his crime being his very existence. There he meets a mysterious young woman named Alice, and the two form a contract. In exchange for helping him out of the Abyss, Oz will help Alice regain her memories.<br /><br />My initial impression after reading this first volume is that this is probably a story that gets better on reread, and I believe there's a lot more foreshadowing going on than I'm aware of. This first volume really is an introduction to the premise, and while we're left off with much more questions than answers, we do have an extremely interesting set up here, that I know will make for a really compelling story. I don't quite feel I have a grasp on the characters, but I really like Oz so far, and how clever he is. As for the art, it's good but not Mochizuki's best, but given how stunning <i>Vanitas</i> is, I know it's going to get a lot better. <br /><br /><a href="https://abookishbalance.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/abookishbalance/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram (main account)</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/renreadsmanga/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram (manga account)</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/abookishbalance" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9916289920967358537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_513535983" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/513535983" />
    <a title="Sophia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16680953-sophia"><img alt="Sophia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376728017p2/16680953.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/513535983?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophia" href="/user/show/16680953-sophia">Sophia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16680953-sophia?shelf=manga-and-comics">manga-and-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16680953-sophia?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer513535983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9627528871388464390">Ok, I first came across this series when I had become up to date with another. I was scrolling down the 'Popular Manga' list and then I saw it. The first thing that got me was the cover. The art on the title page was quite pretty so I decided I'd give it a try. When I first tried reading it, I was sort of confused so I abandoned it for a while. About 4 months later, for lack of anything better to do I tried it again...<br/><br/>BEST.<br/><br/>DECISION.<br/><br/>I.<br/><br/>EVER.<br/><br/>MADE.<br/><br/>IN.<br/><br/>MY.<br/><br/>LIFE.<br/><br/>Although the 1st volume is a tad confusin</span>
  <span id="freeText9627528871388464390" style="display:none">Ok, I first came across this series when I had become up to date with another. I was scrolling down the 'Popular Manga' list and then I saw it. The first thing that got me was the cover. The art on the title page was quite pretty so I decided I'd give it a try. When I first tried reading it, I was sort of confused so I abandoned it for a while. About 4 months later, for lack of anything better to do I tried it again...<br /><br />BEST.<br /><br />DECISION.<br /><br />I.<br /><br />EVER.<br /><br />MADE.<br /><br />IN.<br /><br />MY.<br /><br />LIFE.<br /><br />Although the 1st volume is a tad confusing as you don't get the full picture, the manga overall is amazing. The main protagonist, Oz is likeable (which in my opinion, is quite important because if you don't like the main character the book/series/manga/etc. starts to lose its appeal) as well as the other main characters (Gil, Break, Sharon). I loved how as the manga progressed, in a way you become personally attached to one or more characters. The art is beautiful beyond words. However, the story line is quite complex. It is confusing at first but if you are just patient and keep on reading gradually it will start to make sense. That's one of my favourite things about this manga. Its like when you look at a small segment of a photograph on you computer and at first you think 'WTH?!' but as you zoom out you gradually get to see more of it and eventually the picture starts to become recognisable. There are so many twists in it and when you think you've finally figured something out it turns out to be wrong entirely. <br /><br />If you read it online (like I did), just be aware that the translation is inconsistent, incorrect and confusing at times. The first volume is not the best but just bear with it because it really becomes great as you progress.<br /><br />P.S. This is my 1st review so sorry if it isn't very good....<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9627528871388464390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_605111586" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/605111586" />
    <a title="Isabella" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13440717-isabella"><img alt="Isabella" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442885697p2/13440717.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/605111586?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isabella" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isabella" href="/user/show/13440717-isabella">Isabella</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who can smile</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Isabella by: </span>
      My sister
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13440717-isabella?shelf=cool-powers">cool-powers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13440717-isabella?shelf=never-want-it-to-end">never-want-it-to-end</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13440717-isabella?shelf=key-to-my-heart">key-to-my-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13440717-isabella?shelf=great-plot">great-plot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13440717-isabella?shelf=unique">unique</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13440717-isabella?shelf=great-cover">great-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13440717-isabella?shelf=love-the-hero">love-the-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13440717-isabella?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer605111586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4904814105004047691">First, just let me say that I'm not a fan of manga. I don't hate it, and I'm really glad that some people enjoy it. So, when my sister recommended this to me, I thought, <i>Alright, I'll give it a try to make her happy.</i> Fast-forward two days, and I'm reading the seventh book in the series, biting my nails as I dread the moment when I reach the end.<br/><br/>I just adore the characters, and some of the scenery is very pretty; there <i>is</i> good art in it, even if you don't like anime. The story is long and awesome</span>
  <span id="freeText4904814105004047691" style="display:none">First, just let me say that I'm not a fan of manga. I don't hate it, and I'm really glad that some people enjoy it. So, when my sister recommended this to me, I thought, <i>Alright, I'll give it a try to make her happy.</i> Fast-forward two days, and I'm reading the seventh book in the series, biting my nails as I dread the moment when I reach the end.<br /><br />I just adore the characters, and some of the scenery is very pretty; there <i>is</i> good art in it, even if you don't like anime. The story is long and awesome and convoluted, and I have no idea what's going on but I just know I NEED MORE.<br /><br />I still don't think that I'm a manga fan, but I am definitely a devoted fan of Pandora Hearts. Just for the characters alone, this book gets 5 stars, and I'd give it more if I could.<br /><br />EDIT: Okay, so I just read this review and I can't believe I wrote this. 'Some of the scenery is very pretty' indeed. I've read a lot of manga since reading this, actually, because Pandora Hearts was so beautiful and amazing and perfect that now I read as much manga as I do regular novels, and although some of those authors are good artists, they have nothing on Jun Mochizuki. Her scenery is <i>beautiful,</i> her characters' proportions are <i>real,</i> and her characters' gestures and faces have so much expression that, paired with their amazing, realistic, <i>perfect</i> personalities, this is the only book/series/pretty much anything that can make me cry, laugh, and punch inanimate objects--and it does it on a whim.<br /><br />I cannot explain how sweet, beautiful, heartbreaking, and just <i>amazing</i> this series and this story and these characters are, and I can't explain just how much I love everything about Pandora Hearts.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4904814105004047691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3855249-selena?shelf=manga-manwha">manga-manwha</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3855249-selena?shelf=first-in-series-manga">first-in-series-manga</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3855249-selena?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3855249-selena?shelf=my-must-reads">my-must-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3855249-selena?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3855249-selena?shelf=fairy-tale-retellings">fairy-tale-retellings</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer377733689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6161061007386171075">Much like D.Gray-Man, I picked up the first volume knowing absolutely nothing about it. And just like D.Gray-Man, I can't quite put my finger on just what is so awesome about this. It's so good, but I don't know just what it is I like about it.<br/><br/>I'm going to guess it's the characters. Oz is a goofy kid who gets flung into a strange and dangerous world of magic and monsters. I love these kinds of characters. Oz is a case of a normal person getting involved in chaotic situations through an action th</span>
  <span id="freeText6161061007386171075" style="display:none">Much like D.Gray-Man, I picked up the first volume knowing absolutely nothing about it. And just like D.Gray-Man, I can't quite put my finger on just what is so awesome about this. It's so good, but I don't know just what it is I like about it.<br /><br />I'm going to guess it's the characters. Oz is a goofy kid who gets flung into a strange and dangerous world of magic and monsters. I love these kinds of characters. Oz is a case of a normal person getting involved in chaotic situations through an action that didn't seem a big deal at the time. In his case, it was ditching getting ready for the party, falling in a hole, and taking up a watch. There's something about a prophecy too, but I've found that the former is far more appealing than the latter.<br /><br />Alice is another fun character. She is the exact opposite of the "Alice" we all know from Alice in Wonderland. She's violent, monstrous, and unpredictable. But there's more to her than "I have anger management issues." She has a back-story that seems like it will be revealed slowly throughout the series, and a soft-side that I hope we'll see more of.<br /><br />The story looks interesting. A lot happens in volume one, but it seems more like it's setting up for the rest of the series rather than "this is what the plot will be like."<br /><br />I will be sure to keep reading.<br /><br /><b>Reread 4/18/2020:</b><br /><i>"It all had to be a ridiculous fairy tale written by someone's hand."</i><br /><br />This first volume is a bit chaotic with a lot of characters and concepts introduced one after another. My first impressions above still stand, though. The characters were and are still what draws me in, and it will be interesting to reread knowing how it ends.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6161061007386171075" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20419636-suzanne?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20419636-suzanne?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2700743915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17602724121987007362">This is such a great way to start a series! There's a really good balance between exposition and action here, and I'm honestly impressed by it. I feel like Jun Mochizuki knows exactly how much information to reveal, and how much to withhold. Events start taking off almost immediately, and as a reader, you know just enough to be able to follow them, but you're also really confused as to what's actually happening - which is exactly the point. I've heard that this is a common thread throughout Pand</span>
  <span id="freeText17602724121987007362" style="display:none">This is such a great way to start a series! There's a really good balance between exposition and action here, and I'm honestly impressed by it. I feel like Jun Mochizuki knows exactly how much information to reveal, and how much to withhold. Events start taking off almost immediately, and as a reader, you know just enough to be able to follow them, but you're also really confused as to what's actually happening - which is exactly the point. I've heard that this is a common thread throughout Pandora Hearts, which is apparently filled with constant twists and turns, and I'm really excited to pick up the rest of this series because of it! The characters seem interesting as well, and there seem to be a lot of conflicting interests between them already, which always makes for a great story element in my opinion. In short, I'm intrigued as well as confused in the best way possible, and I'm looking forward to seeing where this story is going!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17602724121987007362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2169645870?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lars" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lars" href="/user/show/73110086-lars">Lars</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73110086-lars?shelf=pandora-hearts">pandora-hearts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2169645870&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2169645870" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3222551763123448715">Pandora Hearts follows the story of a young man named Oz Vessalius, a young noble-to-be who has just turned fifteen. He attends his coming of age ceremony, wherein he's thrown into an alternate dimension called the Abyss, which contains horrible monsters called Chains. His crime, or sin as it is actually called, is apparently his very being. He finds and contracts the most dangerous Chain in the Abyss in order to escape, a young girl called Alice, better known as the B-Rabbit (AKA the Black Bloo</span>
  <span id="freeText3222551763123448715" style="display:none">Pandora Hearts follows the story of a young man named Oz Vessalius, a young noble-to-be who has just turned fifteen. He attends his coming of age ceremony, wherein he's thrown into an alternate dimension called the Abyss, which contains horrible monsters called Chains. His crime, or sin as it is actually called, is apparently his very being. He finds and contracts the most dangerous Chain in the Abyss in order to escape, a young girl called Alice, better known as the B-Rabbit (AKA the Black Bloody Rabbit). She helps him escape in return for his aid in finding her lost memories. After escaping, they meet representatives of Pandora, an organization studying the Abyss and Chains. I enjoyed the story as it's very unique and dark, but with plenty of lighter moments scattered throughout it.<br /><br />The characters are colorful and unique, but they are all very believable. Oz is an eternal optimist, trying everything he can to focus on the positives and be helpful, but is also very childish. Alice is very hot-headed and domineering, but never to the point that she's annoying or truly cruel. They share a strange relationship, but they help balance each other out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3222551763123448715" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('n/ZhzoSXEKyZKwE3vyw79I7OX+eSjLQAiGQX+4hljWmR8TVaciQlBdJiOPdgJuCtgKMFzXMTOVNUoteA9wwAhA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HfvBpHo/dqZ5GsJuU3tVjlDzbDMBV3a7znsi2vAw4L8T/JUwjIxDDzJT+66McY7XXp42GeDI++gSveKhj1ltUg==')})
  }
